مسئلة لا بد للمجاز من قرينة تمنع عن ارادة الحقيقة. المجاز کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ قرینہ موجود ہو جو ارادہ حقیقہ سے مانع ہو۔ پھر یہ خواہ عقلاً ہو یا حسا یا عادة یعنی عرفاً يا شرعاً. وهي اما خارجة الخ یا تو وہ قرینہ ایسا ہوگا جو متکلم اور کلام سے خارج ہوگا ۔ كدلالة المحال جیسے کیمین فور میں دلالت حال قرینہ ہوتا ہے جیسے عورت دروازہ پر نکلنے کے لئے تیار کھڑی ہے خاوند جوش میں آکر کہتا ہے ان خرجت فانت طالق تو یہاں مطلق خروج مراد نہیں ہوگا بلکہ صرف یہی خروج مراد ہوگا جس کے لئے وہ تیار تھی اس کے بعد اگر خروج کرے تو طلاق واقع نہ ہوگی ۔ اد معنی من المتكلم یعنی ایک معنی جو متکلم میں ہے وہ قرینہ مانعہ از حقیقت ہو گا۔ کقولہ تعالیٰ و استفزز من استطعت یہ ابلیس کو خطاب ہے اسی خرک بوسوستک و دعا تك الی الشر من استطعت اور یہاں قرینہ موجود ہے جو مانع ہے اس سے کہ اس امر کے ساتھ حقیقۃ طلب اور ایجاب مراد ہو۔ کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ حکیم ہے اور حکمتہ اس کی صفت ہے لایا مر بالمعصیة معصیت کا حکم نہیں دے گا ـ او لفظ خارج عن هذا الكلام یا قرینہ ایک لفظ ہو گا جو اس کلام سے خارج ہوگا کقولہ تعالی فمن شاء فليومن و من شاء فليكفر تو اس کا حقیقی مفہوم تو تخییر ہے لیکن بعد والا حصہ انا اعتدنا یہ اس کو معنی تخیر سے خارج کر رہا ہے یہ برائے تو بیج وان کار ہے دنحو طلق امرأتی یہ توکیل ہے باعتبار حقیقت کے لیکن ان کتب رجلا نے اس کو توکیل سے خارج کر دیا۔ بلکہ یہ تہدید ہے ۔ اوغیر خارج یعنی وہ قرینه خارج از کلام نہیں ہوگا ۔ خاما ان يكون بعض الافراد اولى یعنی بعض افراد کے اندر اولویتہ موجود ہے اور بعض کے اندر نقص جیسے مملوک سے مکاتب خارج ہوگا کیونکہ اس کے اندر معنی مملوکیتہ ناقص ہے. تو جو رقیق کامل ہے وہی مراد ہوگا۔ اور میکن یا بعض افراد میں اولویتہ نہیں۔
Issue: There must be for majaz a qarina that prevents [the listener from] intending the real meaning. For majaz it is necessary that a qarina exist that prevents the intention of the real meaning. Then it may be intellectual, or sensory, or customary, i.e., conventional or legal. It is either external: i.e., that qarina will be something external to the speaker and the speech, like the indication of the situation; for example, in a mine, the contextual situation is a qarina, like a woman standing ready at the door to go out, and the husband in anger says: 'If you go out, you are divorced.' Here, the absolute going out is not intended, but only that particular go-out for which she was ready. If she goes out after that, divorce will not occur. Or a meaning from the speaker: i.e., a meaning that resides in the speaker and becomes a qarina preventing the real. As Allah's saying: 'And incite' (Quran 17:64) addressing Iblis: 'and incite whoever you can with your voice and call them to evil.' Here, a qarina exists that prevents the real command and obligation from being intended, because Allah is Wise and His wisdom prevents Him from commanding sin. Or a word external to this speech: i.e., the qarina is a word that is outside this speech, like Allah's saying: 'So whoever wills, let him believe, and whoever wills, let him disbelieve' (Quran 18:29). Its real meaning is option, but the later part 'We have prepared for the wrongdoers a fire' removes it from the meaning of option; it is for threat and intimidation. Similarly, 'He said: Divorce my wife' – this is agency (tawkil) in reality, but 'he wrote to a man' removed it from agency; rather, it is a threat. Or not external: i.e., the qarina is not external to the speech. Or that some individuals are more appropriate: i.e., in some individuals there is appropriateness, and in some there is deficiency, like the mukatab is excluded from 'slave' because the meaning of slavery in him is deficient; so the complete slave is intended. And there is no appropriateness in some individuals.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the necessity of a qarina (contextual indicator) for the use of majaz (metaphorical meaning). The text states that to divert from the real (haqiqi) meaning, a qarina must be present that prevents intending the real. The qarina can be of various types: intellectual, sensory, customary (including convention or law). It then classifies qarina into external (to the speaker and speech), such as contextual situation (dilalah al-hal) – e.g., a husband's conditional divorce 'if you go out' when the wife is already at the door; here the qarina restricts the intended go-out. Or a meaning within the speaker – e.g., Allah's address to Iblis 'incite' cannot be a real command because Allah does not command sin; the qarina is Allah's wisdom. Or a word external to the speech – e.g., Quranic verse of choice followed by threat negates option; similarly, 'Divorce my wife' in a written letter is not agency but threat because of the external context. Or not external – i.e., qarina within the speech itself. Or some individuals are more appropriate, like 'slave' primarily refers to a full slave, excluding a mukatab (a slave who has contracted freedom) due to deficiency in the meaning of slavery. This classification helps in interpreting texts correctly in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
قرینہ (qarina): A contextual indicator that prevents the real meaning and allows a metaphorical meaning.
حقیقت (haqiqat): The literal, original meaning of a word.
مجاز (majaz): Metaphorical meaning, requiring a qarina to block the real meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example of a husband saying 'If you go out, you are divorced' while his wife is standing at the door ready to leave, what kind of qarina prevents the absolute meaning of 'go out'?
A) A vocal qarina.
B) A situational qarina (qarina haliyya).
C) A legal qarina.
D) An intellectual qarina.

Key Takeaway
Qarina is essential for any departure from literal meaning in language, and its absence means the literal meaning applies.

Qarina Preventing Literal Meaning in Command
Analyzing how qarina diverts from literal command in Quran and Hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify three types of qarina that prevent the literal meaning of a command and apply the Hanafi principle that a command with a qarina does not indicate obligation.

Core Idea
A command in the Quran is not always obligatory – contextual indicators (qarina) can divert it to permissibility, threat, or non-legal meaning.

This passage from the sharh discusses how qarina (contextual indicator) works in usul al-Fiqh. It provides examples from the Quran and Hadith to illustrate that commands are not always literal obligations. The author distinguishes between qarina external to the speech, qarina based on priority among individuals, and qarina from reason. Understanding this helps in deriving correct rulings from divine texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the concept of qarina
Recognize that qarina is an indicator that prevents the literal meaning of a word from being intended. In the context of commands (amr), it shifts the meaning from obligation to something else.
2
Analyze the first type: qarina from Allah's wisdom
The command to Iblis 'whomever you can' (from Quran 17:64) is not a literal obligation because Allah is Hakim and does not command sin. The qarina of wisdom overrides the literal imperative.
This shows that not every command implies obligation.
3
Analyze the second type: qarina external to the speech
In the verse 'So whoever wills, let him believe...' (Quran 18:29), the literal meaning is choice, but the later part 'We have prepared a fire' provides a qarina that changes it to a threat.
External context can alter the meaning.
4
Analyze the third type: qarina from priority or reason
For hadith like 'Actions are by intentions', the literal meaning (physical actions) is impossible because actions occur without intention. The qarina of reason indicates that the intended meaning is the legal ruling (reward/punishment).
Also, in 'slave' the perfect slave is meant; mukatab is excluded due to deficiency in the meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من استطعت یہ ابلیس کو خطاب ہے اسی خرک بوسوستک [؟] و دعا تک الی الشر من استطعت اور یہاں قرینہ موجود ہے جو مانع ہے اس سے کہ اس امر کے ساتھ حقیقۃ طلب اور ایجاب مراد ہو۔ کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ حکیم ہے اور حکمتہ اس کی صفت ہے لایا مر بالمعصیة معصیت کا حکم نہیں دے گا ـ او لفظ خارج عن هذا الكلام یا قرینہ ایک لفظ ہو گا جو اس کلام سے خارج ہوگا کقولہ تعالی فمن شاء فليومن و من شاء فليكفر تو اس کا حقیقی مفہوم تو تخییر ہے لیکن بعد والا حصہ انا اعتدنا یہ اس کو معنی تخیر سے خارج کر رہا ہے یہ برائے تو بیج وان کار ہے دنحو طلق امرأتی یہ توکیل ہے باعتبار حقیقت کے لیکن ان کتب رجلا نے اس کو توکیل سے خارج کر دیا۔ بلکہ یہ تہدید ہے ۔ اوغیر خارج یعنی وہ قرینه خارج از کلام نہیں ہوگا ۔ خاما ان يكون بعض الافراد اولى یعنی بعض افراد کے اندر اولویتہ موجود ہے اور بعض کے اندر نقص جیسے مملوک سے مکاتب خارج ہوگا کیونکہ اس کے اندر معنی مملوکیتہ ناقص ہے. تو جو رقیق کامل ہے وہی مراد ہوگا۔ اور میکن یا بعض افراد میں اولویتہ نہیں۔ نحو الاعمال بالنيات ورفع عن امتى الخطاء والنسيان اعمال کا لفظہ چونکہ فعل جوارح پر اطلاق ہوتا ہے اور فعل الجوارح کا عین تو نیستہ کے ساتھ نہیں بلکہ بلا ارادہ بھی افعالی جوارح ہوتے ہیں اسی طرح عین خطا اور نسیان مرتفع نہیں بلکہ انسان خطا اور نسیان میں مبتلا رہتا ہے تو معلوم ہوا کہ ان احادیث کے اندر مراد حکم ہے ۔ وجود اعمال اور وجود خطاء مراد نہیں ہے۔
"Whomever you can" This is an address to Iblis. It is [؟] and calling to evil "whomever you can". And here there is a qarina that prevents that this command is meant literally as a request and obligation. Because Allah is Wise and His wisdom is His attribute; He does not command sin. Or a word external to this speech: the qarina is a word that is outside this speech, like His statement: "So whoever wills, let him believe, and whoever wills, let him disbelieve" – its literal meaning is choice, but the latter part "We have prepared" removes it from the meaning of choice; it is for warning, like "he divorced his wife" which is representation (tawkeel) literally, but "a man wrote" removed it from representation; rather it is a threat. Or not external: meaning the qarina is not external to the speech. So it is that some individuals are more appropriate: meaning in some individuals there is priority and in some deficiency, like a mukatab is excluded from a slave because the meaning of slavery in him is deficient; so the perfect slave is meant. Or [makin] there is no priority in some individuals. Like "actions are by intentions" and "my nation is forgiven for mistake and forgetfulness" – the word "actions" is applied to actions of the limbs, and the actual actions of the limbs are not with intention, but actions of the limbs occur without intention; similarly the actual mistake and forgetfulness are not removed, rather a person remains afflicted with mistake and forgetfulness. So it is known that in these hadith, the ruling (hukm) is meant; the existence of actions and the existence of mistake are not meant.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage discusses how a qarina (contextual indicator) can prevent the literal meaning of a command (amr) from being understood as an obligation. The author gives examples: the Quranic address to Iblis 'whomever you can' is not a literal command because Allah's wisdom precludes commanding sin. Another type of qarina is a word outside the speech, like 'so whoever wills...' where later context shows it is a threat, not a choice. A third type is a qarina not external but based on priority among individuals: a mukatab (slave with contract) is excluded from the term 'slave' in legal rulings due to deficiency. Finally, hadith like 'actions are by intentions' are analyzed: the literal existence of actions is not intended; rather, the ruling (reward/punishment) is intended, because actions without intention still exist. This shows that qarina can shift meaning from literal to legal.

Key Terms
قرینہ (qarina): An indicator or context that prevents the literal meaning of a word from being intended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because it is a metaphorical statement
D) Because it is abrogated

Key Takeaway
A qarina prevents the literal meaning of a command; identifying qarina is essential for correct istinbat in Hanafi usul.

Examples of Majaz and Classification of Qarina
Examples of majaz and classification of qarina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify qarina in legal texts, classify it as external or internal to speech, and explain how it diverts from literal to metaphorical meaning.

Core Idea
A qarina (indicator) in speech overrides literal meaning, directing to a metaphorical or intended meaning.

This lesson builds on the concept of majaz (metaphorical usage) by providing concrete examples from Hanafi fiqh, such as oaths and agency contracts, where literal meanings are abandoned due to custom or legal prohibition. It then presents a systematic classification of qarina—the indicator that triggers the shift from literal to metaphorical interpretation. Understanding this classification is essential for correctly interpreting legal texts, especially when a word may have multiple applications.

Guided Path
1
Identify literal meaning and abandoned custom
For each example, note the literal meaning and why it is abandoned (custom or legal prohibition).
2
Recognize intended metaphorical meaning
Determine the intended meaning that is reasonable in context.
3
Locate the qarina
Identify what indicator (custom, legal prohibition, etc.) forces the shift.
4
Classify the qarina
Using the classification, decide if the qarina is external or internal to speech, and if internal, whether it is from the same speech or another.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونحو لا يا كل من هذه النخلة ولا ياكل من هذا الدقيق ولا يشرب من هذا البیر ان کی حقیقت تو یہ ہے کہ کھجور کے تنے کو کھائے یہ معجور حساد عادہ ہے اور خود آٹا منہ میں پھانکے اور خود منہ و زبان کے ساتھ بغیر کسی آلہ کے بیر سے پانی پیتے یہ سب عادة متروک ہیں اس لئے یہاں مجاز مراد ہوگا یعنی کھجور کا پھل کھانا آٹے سے پکی ہوئی روٹی وغیرہ کھانا اور بیر سے ہاتھوں کے ساتھ یا کسی برتن کے ساتھ پینا مراد ہوگا ۔ جب مجاز مراد ہو چکا تو اب حقیقت مراد نہیں ہو سکتی ۔ حتی اذا استف یعنی آٹے کو پھانکتا ہے۔ رکوع یعنی کنویں سے خود منہ لگا کر پیتا ہے تو حانث نہیں ہوگا۔ و نحو لا يضع قدمہ میں حقیقی مفہوم یعنی دار سے باہر لیٹ کر قدم لمبے کر کے دار میں داخل کرے یہ حقیقہ عادة مھجور ہے لہذا یہ مجازہ انہ دخول ہوگا کیف ما کان و کالا سماء المنقوله اور جیسے اسماء منقولہ ہیں کہ ان حقیقی معنی عرفاً متروک ہو چکا ہے جیسے دابتہ کا حقیقی مفہوم ما يدب علی الارض متروک ہو چکا ہے اور عرفا اس کی استعمال مخصوص طور پر فرس میں ہو چکی ہے تو سی مجاز لغوی مراد رہے گا اور حقیقی لغو یہ مراد نہیں ۔ اسی طرح منقولات شرعیہ اور اصطلاحیہ کہ ان کے اندر حقیقہ لغویہ متروک ہو چکی ہے ۔ رنحو التوكيل بالمخصوصة اس کاحقیقی مفہوم تو خصومہ و جھگڑا کرتا ہے حق و ناحق کو نہیں دیکھنا اور اس قسم کی خصومت شرعاً محجور ہے خانہ بصرف الى مطلق الجواب یعنی مطلق جواب مراد ہوگا ۔ خواہ بالاقرار ہو یا بالا نکار جیسے حق نظر آئے لان معناها الحقيقي یعنی حق ہو یا باطل جھگڑنا ہی جھگڑنا یہ شرعاً مھجور اور ممنوع ہے اور مجور شرع بمنزلہ مھجور عادی کے ہوتا ہے لہذا حقیقی مفہوم مراد نہیں ہوگا ۔ نیتناول الاقرار والا نکار یعنی خواہ وکیل اقرار علی الموکل کرے یا انکار دونو کو یہ توکیل شامل ہوگی یہ مقصد نہیں ہے کہ صرف انکار پر اصرار کرے کیونکہ یہ شرعاً ممنوع ہے جب کہ یہ جھوٹ پرمشتمل ہو۔ اعلم ان القرينة قرينة مختلف اقسام پر ہے جسکے امثلہ ما قبل میں مذکور ہیں حاصل تقسیم یہ ہے کہ قرینہ یا تو خارج از متکلم اور خارج از کلام ہوگا۔ یعنی وہ جنس کلام سے نہیں ہوگا۔ ای لاتکون اس کی تفصیل کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ وہ معنی فی المتكلم نہ ہو یعنی صفتہ قائمہ بالمتکلم نہ ہو اور جنس کلام سے نہ ہو یہ مراد ہے خارج از متکلم و از کلام ہونے کی ۔ او تکون یا معنی فی المتکلم ہو گا یعنی صفتہ قائمہ بالمتكلم جیسے ذلت حکیم کے ساتھ قیام وصف حکمتہ ہے او تكون من جس الكلام یا جنس کلام سے ہوگا ۔ ثم هذه القرينة پھر یہ قرینہ جو جنس کلام سے ہوگا یا تو لفظ ہوگا جو اس کلام سے خارج ہوگا جو مشتمل على المجاز ہے بل يكون فی کلام آخر بلکہ دوسری کلام کا حصہ ہوگا اور یہی لفظ خارج قرینہ ہو گا جو دال ہو گا کہ ارادہ حقیقہ نہیں ہے او غير خارج عن هذا الكلام يا اس کلام سے خارج نہیں بلکہ وہ قرینہ لفظی خود اسی کلام کا عین ہوگا اوشی منه یا اس کلام کا حصہ اور جز ہوگا جو عدم ارادہ حقیقت پر دال ہوگا تم هذا القسم علی نوعین یعنی به قرینه جو خارج از کلام نہیں ہے یہ دو قسم پر ہے اما ان يكون بعض الافراد اولى يا تو بعض افراد اول بالصدق ہیں من البعض الآخر
And like 'do not eat from this date-palm' and 'do not eat from this flour' and 'do not drink from this well': its literal meaning is to eat the trunk of the date-palm, which is an abandoned custom, and to stuff flour into the mouth, and to drink from the well directly with mouth and tongue without any vessel – all these are abandoned customs. Therefore, the metaphorical meaning is intended: to eat the fruit of the date-palm, to eat bread made from flour, and to drink from the well with hands or a vessel. When the metaphorical meaning is intended, the literal cannot be intended. So if one swallows flour (stuffing) or drinks from the well by putting mouth to it (leaning), he does not break the oath. And like 'do not place his foot' – its literal meaning is to lie outside the house and stretch the leg inside; that literal practice is abandoned, so it is metaphorical for entering in any manner. And like transferred names (asma munqala): their literal meaning has been abandoned customarily, e.g., the literal meaning of 'dābba' is 'that which crawls on the earth' but it has been abandoned, and customarily it is used specifically for a horse; so the metaphorical (customary) meaning is intended, not the lexical literal. Similarly, shar'i and technical transferred terms have their lexical literal abandoned. And like 'tawkeel with mukhasimah' (appointing for litigation): its literal meaning is to quarrel, not caring about right or wrong, and such quarrel is legally prohibited. So it is turned to absolute response, whether by admission or denial, as right appears. Because its literal meaning — quarreling whether right or wrong — is legally abandoned and forbidden, and legally prohibited is like customarily abandoned. Hence the literal meaning is not intended. It includes admission and denial: whether the agent admits against the principal or denies, the tawkeel includes both; the purpose is not to insist on denial only, because that is legally forbidden when it involves lying. Know that qarina is of various types, examples of which were mentioned before. The summary of the division is: qarina is either external to the speaker and external to the speech, i.e., it is not from the genre of speech. Its explanation: it is not a meaning in the speaker (i.e., not an attribute subsisting in the speaker) and not from the genre of speech — this is what is meant by being external to speaker and speech. Or it is a meaning in the speaker, like an attribute subsisting in the speaker, e.g., the attribute of wisdom subsisting in the Wise (Allah). Or it is from the genre of speech. Then this qarina which is from the genre of speech is either a word external to this speech (i.e., part of another speech) indicating that the literal meaning is not intended, or not external to this speech, but the verbal qarina is the very same speech or part of it, indicating non-intent of the literal meaning. Then this latter section is divided into two types: either some individuals are more appropriate (awla bil-sidq) than others.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage provides multiple examples where a qarina (context) forces a metaphorical meaning, and then concludes with a classification of qarina. The examples: oaths about not eating from a tree/drinking from a well – literal is abandoned custom, so meaning is figurative. Similarly, 'do not place foot' – literal stretching leg is abandoned, so means entering. Transferred names like 'dābba' – lexical meaning abandoned, customary meaning used. For tawkeel (agency) in litigation, literal meaning (quarreling) is legally prohibited, so it means general response. The classification: qarina can be external (outside speaker and speech, like wisdom of Allah) or internal (meaning in speaker, or from the speech itself). The internal qarina from speech can be a separate word (external to this speech) or part of this speech. When it is part of this speech, it may indicate that some individuals are more apt to be included, like when a term has primary and secondary applications.

Key Terms
قرینہ (qarina): An indicator that prevents literal meaning and diverts to metaphorical or appropriate meaning.
مجاز (majaz): Metaphorical usage where literal meaning is abandoned due to qarina or custom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the oath 'I will not eat from this date-palm,' why is the literal meaning (eating the trunk) not intended?
A) Because the trunk is not edible
B) Because it is an abandoned custom
C) Because the text is metaphorical
D) Because the speaker is not serious

Key Takeaway
Qarina is a crucial tool for interpreting legal texts, guiding the jurist to the correct intended meaning when literal meaning is impossible or abandoned.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
12 min
Classification of Qarīnah and Its Types
Classification of qarīnah into eight divisions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify qarīnah into its eight divisions and apply each type to identify when a word is used metaphorically (majāz) rather than literally.

Core Idea
Qarīnah is not just external context; it can be embedded in the speaker's attribute or in the word's own priority in truthfulness.

The text presents a comprehensive eight-way classification of qarīnah (contextual evidence). This system is essential for determining when a word is used metaphorically in the Quran, hadith, and legal rulings. You will learn the primary divisions—external to speaker/speech, internal to speaker, and from the speech itself—and the crucial sub-distinction between a mukhassis and a qarīnah. Mastering this classification will sharpen your ability to derive rulings from texts that are not literal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary division of qarīnah
The text divides qarīnah into three broad categories: (1) external to the speaker and external to the speech, (2) a meaning/attribute in the speaker (e.g., wisdom), and (3) from the genre of the speech itself.
Categories 1 and 2 are non-verbal; category 3 is verbal.
2
Analyze the verbal qarīnah subdivisions
Verbal qarīnah is further split into (a) a word external to the current speech (another part of discourse) and (b) a word within the same speech (the word itself or its part). The latter has two types: (i) some individuals are prior in truthfulness (awlā bi al-ṣidq) and (ii) no individual priority, as in 'innamā al-a'mālu bil-niyyāt'.
Type (b)(i) is the focus of a dispute: is it a mukhassis or a qarīnah?
3
Distinguish mukhassis from qarīnah
The text clarifies that a verbal mukhassis explicitly imposes a contradictory ruling, while a qarīnah merely indicates that the literal meaning is not intended. Priority in truthfulness is not explicit exclusion, so it is a qarīnah, not a mukhassis.
This distinction affects how we derive rulings from general words.
4
Examine the examples of rational, customary, and sensory qarīnah
The text provides examples: in the oath of immediacy (common custom), in 'faman shā'a falyu'min' (rational—choice cannot coexist with threat), in 'ṭalliq imra'atī' (custom), and in the hadith of intentions (rational). Each prevents the literal meaning.
These examples demonstrate that qarīnah can be non-verbal (custom, reason) or verbal (priority).

من جس الكلام یا جنس کلام سے ہوگا ۔ ثم هذه القرينة پھر یہ قرینہ جو جنس کلام سے ہوگا یا تو لفظ ہوگا جو اس کلام سے خارج ہوگا جو مشتمل على المجاز ہے بل يكون فی کلام آخر بلکہ دوسری کلام کا حصہ ہوگا اور یہی لفظ خارج قرینہ ہو گا جو دال ہو گا کہ ارادہ حقیقہ نہیں ہے او غير خارج عن هذا الكلام يا اس کلام سے خارج نہیں بلکہ وہ قرینہ لفظی خود اسی کلام کا عین ہوگا اوشی منه یا اس کلام کا حصہ اور جز ہوگا جو عدم ارادہ حقیقت پر دال ہوگا تم هذا القسم علی نوعین یعنی به قرینه جو خارج از کلام نہیں ہے یہ دو قسم پر ہے اما ان يكون بعض الافراد اولى يا تو بعض افراد اول بالصدق ہیں من البعض الآخر جیسے ہم نے تخصیص کہ مسئلہ میں ذکر کیا ہے کہ ان المخصص کہ مخصص کبھی یہ ہوتا ہے کہ بعض افراد صدق لفظ میں اول من البعض ہوتے ہیں مثلا بعض افراد ناقص فی الصدق ہیں اور بعض افراد زائد فی الصدق ہیں۔ فاذا قال كل مملوك لي حد تو یہ مکاتب کو شامل نہیں ہو گا حالانکہ مکاتب حقیقة مملوک ہے۔ فيكون هذا كل يه اللفظ توپ یہ لفظ بحیثت مقصور علی البعض ہونے کے مجاز ہوگا یعنی غیر مکاتب کو شامل رہیگا۔ اولم یکن بعض الافراد اولی یہ جیسے انما الاعمال بالنیات میں تھا۔ فانحصرت القرينة في هذه الاقسام الثمانية . فان قيس قد جعا في فصل التخصيص حاصل سوال یه که فصل تخصیص میں بعض افراد کا اولی من البعض ہونا مخصص غیر کلامی کا قسم بین یا گیا ہے ۔ دھجنا اور اس مقام پر اسے قرینہ لفظیہ کا قسم بنایا گیا ہے یعنی یہ قرینہ کلامی ہوا - نص الفرق بينهما الى بين المخصص والقرنة قلنا یہ جواب ہے حاصل یہ کہ مخصص کلامی سے مراد یہ ہے که کلام صریح طور پر بعض افراد میں ایسے حکم کو واجب کرے جو اس حکم کے مناقض ہو جس کو عام نے واجب کیا تھا اور ہر مخصص جو ایسا نہ ہو یعنی صریح نہ ہو وہ مخصص کلامی نہیں ہوتا۔ اب بعض افراد کا اولی ہونا یہ اس تفسیر کے ساتھ مخصص غیر کلامی ہوگا ۔ دھینا اور اس مقام پر قرینہ لفظیہ سے مراد یہ ہے کہ لفظ سے سمجھ میں آئے جس طریقہ پر بھی ہو کہ حقیقت۔ یہاں مراد نہیں ہے اس کو ہم قرینہ لفظیہ کہتے ہیں ۔ دنی کل مملوک کی حد تو لفظ مملوک سے سمجھ آتا ہے کہ یہ مکاتب کو شامل نہیں ہے کیونکہ مکاتب میں مملوکیتہ ناقص ہے ۔ جثنا الى الامثله المذكورة متن میں ہر قسم قرینہ کی مثال اس کے بعد ذکر کر دی ہے لیکن ہم نے یہ ذکر نہیں کیا تھا کہ قریہ مانعہ عن ارادة الحقيقة عقد ہے یا حسايا عادة وشرعاً فتبين مهنا هذا المعنى اور میں اس مقام پر بیان کرتے ہیں فنی یمین الفور یعنی یمین فور میں کہ جب عورت ارادہ خروج کا کرتی ہے اور خاوندا سے کہتا ہے ان خرجت فانت طالق تو اس کو فور پر محمول کریں گے یعنی اس کہنے کے بعد اگر فوراً اور بلا تاخیر خروج کرے تو مطلقہ ہوگی ورنہ تو نہیں ۔ اور یہاں جو قرینہ مانع عن ارادة الحقیقہ ہے وہ عرف عام ہے کہ یہی خروج مخصوص مراد ہے۔ حقیقی مفہوم یعنی خروج مطلق مراد نہیں ہے ۔ دنی تولیہ تعالی را ستعزز من استطعت میں قرینہ جو ارادہ حقیقت سے مانع ہے وہ عملاً ہے اور اسی طرح اللہ تعالیٰ کے قول فمن شاء فلیو من میں قرینہ عقلیہ کیونکہ اس کا حقیقی مفہوم یعنی تخییر اور ادھر انا اعتدنا للظالمین نارا سے جو عذاب مستفاد ہوتا ہے۔ ان کا اجتماع عقلا ممتنع ہے تو معلوم ہوا کہ تخییر مراد نہیں ہے ورنہ تو عذاب کی وعید لاحق نہ ہوتی . وفي قوله طلق امرأتى ان كنت رجله الحقيقة يعني التوكيل ممتنع عرفا عني عرف عام اس سے توکیل نہیں سمجھتا بلکہ دھمکی سمجھتا ہے۔ وفی قولہ علیہ السلام الاعمال بالنیات میں قرینہ عقلیہ ہے کہ حقیقہ یعنی وجود الاعمال مراد نہیں ہے بلکہ ثواب الاعمال مراد ہے اور لا یا کل من بندہ النخلہ ا والدقیق میں قرینه حمید اور لا یشرب من ہذا البیر میں حسی اور عرفی قرینہ موجود ہے لا یضع قدمہ میں عربی قرینہ اور اسماء منقوله
And he does not drink from this well — its reality is that he eats the trunk of the date palm, this is abandoned custom, and he stuffs flour in his mouth himself and drinks water from the well with his mouth and tongue without any utensil; all these are abandoned customs. Therefore, here metaphorical meaning is intended: meaning eating the fruit of the date palm, eating bread made from flour, and drinking from the well with hands or a vessel. Since metaphorical meaning is intended, literal meaning cannot be intended. So if he stuffs flour or drinks by putting his mouth to the well, he does not incur the oath. And similarly, 'do not place his foot' — the literal meaning is that he lies outside the house and extends his foot into the house; this custom is abandoned, so it is metaphorical for entering in any manner. And like transferred nouns: their literal meaning is customarily abandoned, e.g., 'dābbah' literally means 'what crawls on the earth' but customarily used only for horse, so the metaphorical linguistic meaning remains, not the literal. Similarly, religious and technical transferred terms have their linguistic literal meaning abandoned. And like 'al-tawkeel bi al-mukhāṣamah': its literal meaning is argumentation, not caring about right or wrong; such argumentation is legally prohibited, so it is turned to absolute response, whether by admission or denial. Because its literal meaning – arguing whether right or wrong – is legally prohibited, and what is legally prohibited is like what is customarily abandoned. So the literal meaning is not intended; it includes admission and denial by the agent. The purpose is not to insist on denial because that is prohibited when it involves falsehood. Know that qarīnah is of various types, examples of which were mentioned earlier. The summary of the division is that qarīnah is either external to the speaker and external to the speech, i.e., it is not from the genre of speech. Explaining that: it is not a meaning in the speaker, i.e., not an attribute subsisting in the speaker, and not from the genre of speech – this is what is meant by external to speaker and speech. Or it is a meaning in the speaker, i.e., an attribute subsisting in the speaker, like the attribute of wisdom subsisting in the wise. Or it is from the genre of speech. Then this qarīnah that is from the genre of speech is either a word that is external to that speech which contains the metaphor, but rather it is part of another speech, and this external word is a qarīnah indicating that the literal meaning is not intended; or it is not external to this speech, rather it is the very word of this speech or part of it, indicating non-intention of the literal meaning. Then this division is of two types: either some individuals are prior in truthfulness over others – as we mentioned in the discussion of specification: sometimes the mukhassis is that some individuals are prior in truthfulness of the word over others, e.g., some individuals are deficient in truthfulness and some are excessive. So if he says 'every slave of mine is free up to a limit', that does not include the mukātab even though the mukātab is literally a slave. So this word 'all' becomes metaphorical in the sense of being restricted to some, i.e., it includes only non-mukātab slaves. Or some individuals are not prior – like in 'actions are by intentions'. Thus the qarīnah is confined to these eight divisions. If it is asked: in the chapter of specification, the priority of some individuals over others was made a division of non-verbal mukhassis; here it is made a division of verbal qarīnah, i.e., it becomes verbal qarīnah. The difference between mukhassis and qarīnah is: we say the answer is that by verbal mukhassis is meant that the speech explicitly imposes on some individuals a ruling that contradicts the ruling imposed by the general word. Every mukhassis that is not like that – i.e., not explicit – is not verbal mukhassis. So the priority of some individuals, with this interpretation, is a non-verbal mukhassis. And here by verbal qarīnah is meant that it is understood from the word, in whatever manner, that the literal meaning is not intended; we call that verbal qarīnah. So 'every slave of mine is free up to a limit' – the word 'slave' indicates that it does not include the mukātab because his slavery is deficient. Then we come to the examples mentioned in the text: each type of qarīnah has been given an example. But we had not mentioned whether the qarīnah preventing the literal meaning is rational, customary, or legal. So here we explain that. In the oath of immediacy: when a woman intends to go out and the husband says 'if you go out, you are divorced', it is construed as immediate: if she goes out immediately without delay, she is divorced, otherwise not. Here the qarīnah preventing the literal meaning is common custom – that only this specific exit is meant, not the absolute literal meaning of exit. And in the words of Allah exalted 'fa man shā'a falyu'min' the qarīnah preventing the literal meaning is rational, because the literal meaning of choice and the punishment mentioned in 'innā a‘tadnā li al-ẓālimīna nārā' cannot rationally coexist; so it is known that choice is not intended, otherwise the threat of punishment would not follow. And in his saying 'divorce my wife if you are a man' – the literal meaning of agency is customarily impossible; common custom does not understand agency from it but rather a threat. And in the saying of the Prophet (ﷺ) 'actions are by intentions' the qarīnah is rational: the literal meaning (the existence of actions) is not intended, rather the reward of actions. And in 'lā yākul min bunduq al-nakhlah wā al-daqīq' there is a customary qarīnah; in 'wa lā yashrab min hādhā al-bīr' there is a sensory and customary qarīnah; in 'lā yaḍa‘ qadamah' there is a customary qarīnah; and in transferred nouns there is customary qarīnah.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage is a detailed classification of qarīnah (contextual evidence) in the context of majāz. The author begins by revisiting earlier examples where the literal meaning (ḥaqīqah) has been abandoned by custom, thus requiring metaphorical interpretation. Examples include eating dates, drinking from a well, placing a foot, and transferred nouns like 'dābbah'. He then states that qarīnah is of various types. The primary division is: qarīnah either (1) external to the speaker and external to the speech, (2) a meaning in the speaker (an attribute subsisting in the speaker, e.g., wisdom), or (3) from the genre of speech. The third type (from the genre of speech) is further subdivided into (a) a word external to the speech (i.e., from another speech) or (b) the word itself or part of it. The latter (b) is of two kinds: (i) where some individuals are prior in truthfulness (awla bi al-sidq) over others – like 'every slave of mine is free up to a limit' excludes the mukātab because his slavery is deficient, so the word 'slave' is used metaphorically to exclude him; and (ii) where no individual is prior – like 'actions are by intentions' where the qarīnah is rational, indicating that reward is meant, not the physical existence of actions. The author then addresses a potential objection: in the chapter of specification (takhṣīṣ), the priority of some individuals was classified as a non-verbal mukhāṣṣiṣ, whereas here it is classified as a verbal qarīnah. He resolves this by distinguishing between mukhāṣṣiṣ and qarīnah: a verbal mukhāṣṣiṣ imposes an explicit contradictory ruling, whereas qarīnah is merely indicative of non-literal intention. Thus priority of individuals is non-verbal mukhāṣṣiṣ in the specification discussion, but here it is considered a verbal qarīnah because it is understood from the word itself. Finally, the author provides examples of different types of qarīnah that prevent literal meaning: in the oath of immediacy (yamīn al-fawr), the qarīnah is common custom; in the verse 'fa man shā'a falyu'min', it is rational (impossibility of coexistence of choice and threat); in the saying 'ṭalliq imra’atī in kunta rajulahā', it is custom (understood as threat, not agency); in the hadith 'innamā al-a‘mālu bil-niyyāt', it is rational; and in the examples of eating, drinking, and placing foot, the qarīnah is customary and sensory. This passage is a cornerstone for understanding how Hanafi usul uses qarīnah to identify majāz, distinguishing it from ḥaqīqah and from mukhāṣṣiṣ.

Key Terms
القرینة (al-qarīnah): Contextual evidence that indicates the intended meaning is not literal but metaphorical
المجاز (al-majāz): Metaphorical usage where the word is used for other than its original meaning due to a qarīnah
اولی بالصدق (awlā bi al-ṣidq): Some individuals of a word are more deserving of truthfulness than others, indicating metaphorical limitation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification, which of the following is NOT a type of qarīnah?
A) Qarīnah external to speaker and speech
B) Qarīnah that is a meaning (attribute) in the speaker
C) Qarīnah that is a separate verse of the Quran
D) Qarīnah from the genre of speech (verbal)

Key Takeaway
Qarīnah is a multifaceted concept in Hanafi usul; it can be external, internal, or verbal, and priority in truthfulness (awlā bi al-ṣidq) is a verbal qarīnah, not an explicit mukhassis.

Eight Types of Qarina Preventing Literal Meaning
Classifying qarina that prevent literal intent into eight types with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and classify the eight types of qarina that prevent literal meaning, and distinguish between a qarina and a mukhassis in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
A qarina prevents literal intent; Hanafi usul identifies eight types—custom, reason, action, sensory, legal, and more.

The Hanafi school recognizes that contextual indicators (qarina) can prevent the literal meaning (haqiqah) of a word from being intended. Understanding these indicators is crucial for correctly interpreting legal texts. In this lesson, we explore the eight types of qarina classified by Hanafi usul scholars, with examples from the Qur'an, hadith, and everyday oaths. We also clarify the boundary between a qarina and a verbal specifier (mukhassis kalami), a point that often causes confusion.

Guided Path
1
Understand the mukhassis vs qarina distinction
First, grasp the Hanafi criterion: a mukhassis kalami explicitly imposes a ruling contradictory to the general term, while a qarina only indicates that the literal meaning is not intended without explicit contradiction.
This distinction is the foundation for classifying qarina types.
2
Enumerate the eight qarina types
From the text, list the eight types: 'urf 'amm (general custom), 'amal (action), 'aql (reason), 'urf again in threat context, 'aql in 'actions by intentions', hiss (sensory), 'urf (customary), and shar' (legal). Note that 'urf appears in multiple examples.
Each type originates from a different source: custom, action, rational inference, sensory perception, or divine law.
3
Analyze each example's qarina source
For each example in the passage, identify which type of qarina is operative and explain how it prevents the literal intent.
For instance, in the oath of immediacy, general custom dictates that the going out is immediate, not absolute.
4
Apply the classification to a new scenario
Take a statement like 'I will not eat from this tree' and determine if a qarina is present; use the text's reasoning to decide whether it's sensory or customary.
Consider whether the item is customarily eaten; if not, the qarina may be customary.
5
Evaluate the debate on priority of individuals
Review the objection and response: the priority of some individuals in truthfulness (ba'd al-afrad awla) is a qarina, not a mukhassis, because it does not explicitly contradict the general ruling.
This clarifies the boundary between takhsis and qarina.

As we mentioned in the issue of takhsis, that the mukhassis sometimes is that some individuals are prior in the truth of the word, e.g. some individuals are deficient in truthfulness and some are excessive in truthfulness. So if he says 'every slave of mine is freed', this will not include the mukatab although the mukatab is truly a slave. So this 'every' word, due to being restricted to some individuals, becomes metaphorical, i.e. it will include non-mukatab. Or it is that some individuals are prior, like in the hadith 'actions are by intentions'. So the qarina is restricted to these eight categories. If it is said: He made in the chapter of takhsis the answer: the question is that in the chapter of takhsis, the priority of some individuals over others is made a type of non-verbal mukhassis. And here it is made a type of verbal qarina, i.e. this is a verbal qarina. Text: the difference between the two, between the mukhassis and the qarina. We say: this is an answer. The summary is that by verbal mukhassis is meant that the speech explicitly makes incumbent on some individuals a ruling that contradicts the ruling that the general term made incumbent. And every mukhassis that is not like that, i.e. not explicit, is not a verbal mukhassis. Now the priority of some individuals, according to this interpretation, will be a non-verbal mukhassis. And here by verbal qarina is meant that it is understood from the word in whatever way that the reality (is not intended). We call this a verbal qarina. Thus, in 'every slave of mine is freed', from the word 'slave' it is understood that it does not include the mukatab because the slavery of the mukatab is deficient. Then we come to the examples mentioned in the text: every type of qarina's example is mentioned thereafter. But we had not mentioned that the qarina preventing the intended literal meaning is a contract or sensory or customary or legal. So this meaning is explained here. And I am explaining at this place: For the oath of immediacy (yamin al-fawr), when a woman intends to go out and her husband says to her 'If you go out, you are divorced', we will interpret it as immediate, meaning that if she goes out immediately after his saying, without delay, she will be divorced; otherwise not. And the qarina here preventing the intended literal meaning is general custom that this specific going out is intended. The real meaning, i.e. absolute going out, is not intended. And in the saying of Allah 'wa-staz'az man istata'ta' the qarina preventing the intended reality is action ('amalan). And similarly in Allah's saying 'fa man sha'a falyu'min' the qarina is rational, because its real meaning is choice, and on the other hand, from 'inna a'tadna liz-zalimina nara' the punishment is understood. Their combination rationally is impossible. So it is known that choice is not intended; otherwise the threat of punishment would not follow. And in his saying 'Tallaq imra'ati in kunta rajul' the reality means agency is prevented by custom; general custom does not understand agency from this but understands threat. And in the Prophet's saying 'al-a'malu bin-niyyat' the qarina is rational, because the reality, i.e. the existence of actions, is not intended; rather the reward of actions is intended. And in 'la ya'kulu min hadhihi an-nakhlah' the qarina is sensory, and in 'la yashrabu min hadha al-bi'r' the qarina is sensory and customary. In 'la yada'u qadamahu' the qarina is customary. And in transferred names (asma' manqula), sometimes general custom like the word 'rabba' or specific custom i.e. particular terminology like 'salat' etc., and in agency for litigation (tawkil bil-khusuma) the qarina is legal, because absolute litigation is prohibited; only litigation by right is permissible. If it is said: We do not accept that the real meaning is prevented in the saying 'la ya'kulu min hadhihi an-nakhlah', i.e. in this speech we do not accept that there is a sensory qarina preventing the intended reality, because the subject of the oath is the non-eating of the date palm, and non-eating is not sensorily impossible; rather non-eating is correct. Indeed, its eating is prohibited, not non-eating. We say: The oath, when it enters on a negation, prohibits what was not prohibited. So the effect of the oath is that the thing is prohibited only because of the oath. And that which is not customarily eaten is not prohibited by the oath. Therefore, now it is a prohibition of eating, not of non-eating.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the types of qarina (contextual indicators) that prevent the literal meaning (haqiqah) from being intended. The author first addresses a confusion about the classification of 'priority of some individuals in truthfulness' (ba'd al-afrad awla) — whether it is a mukhassis (specifier) or a qarina. He clarifies that a verbal mukhassis must explicitly impose a contradictory ruling, while a non-verbal mukhassis does not. Then he lists eight types of qarina, giving examples: 'urf 'amm (general custom) in oath of immediacy, 'amal (action) in the verse 'wa-staz'az', 'aql (rational) in 'fa man sha'a', 'urf again in threats, 'aql in 'al-a'malu bin-niyyat', hiss (sensory) and 'urf in 'la ya'kulu min hadhihi an-nakhlah', and shar' (legal) in agency for litigation. He then defends the inclusion of the sensory qarina in 'la ya'kulu' against an objection, explaining that the oath negates the customarily eaten item, not the absolute non-eating. The discussion follows the Hanafi usul framework where qarina determines whether haqiqah or majaz is intended.

Key Terms
قرینہ (qarina): A contextual indicator that prevents the literal meaning from being intended, guiding to a metaphorical or specific meaning.
مخصص کلامی (mukhassis kalami): A specifier that explicitly imposes a ruling contradictory to the general term.
حقیقت (haqiqah): The literal, original meaning of a word.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a qarina prevents literal meaning without explicitly contradicting the general ruling, and its types arise from custom, reason, action, senses, and law.

Conjunction Type and Legal Effect: 'Atf Jumal vs 'Atf Mufrad
Exploring how 'atf type changes legal outcomes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between 'atf jumal and 'atf mufrad in legal utterances and apply the Hanafi rule that a changer (mugir) operates only in immediate conjunction.

Core Idea
Grammatical conjunction type determines whether later words retroactively alter earlier ones.

In Hanafi usul, the form of a legal utterance can change the ruling. This passage explores why a master's separate sentences freeing two slave-girls yield a different result than a single permission to marry two sisters. The key lies in whether the conjunction joins whole sentences ('atf jumal) or individual words ('atf mufrad). Understanding this distinction sharpens your ability to parse legal speech correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two cases: two slave-girls (امتین) freed separately, and two sisters (اختین) given a single marriage permission. Read the utterances given for each case.
2
Classify the conjunction type
For slave-girls: 'هذه حرة وهذه حرة' – two independent sentences, i.e. 'atf jumal. For sisters: 'أجزت نكاح هذه وهذه' – one verb with two direct objects, i.e. 'atf mufrad.
The key is whether the second element shares the same governor (verb) as the first.
3
Determine independence vs. dependence
In 'atf jumal, each sentence stands alone; the second does not affect the first. In 'atf mufrad, the second word is part of the same act (e.g., permission), so the first depends on the second for completion.
This is why the second sentence cannot be a 'mugir' (changer) in the slave-girl case.
4
Apply the rule to hypotheticals
The passage tests the boundary: if separate permissions are given for sisters, the first is valid; if a single conjoined phrase is used for slave-girls, both are freed together. This confirms the rule is purely linguistic.
This shows the difference is not substantive but stems from the formulation (وضع).
5
State the Hanafi usul rule
When a later statement retroactively changes the first, it must be متصل (immediately connected). In 'atf jumal, the second sentence is not connected to the first in that sense, so no change occurs. In 'atf mufrad, the words are inseparable, so change is possible.
This rule helps in interpreting contracts, wills, and other legal documents.

Source Text

هے امافی الاختین یعنی احتین والے مسئلہ میں نکاح ثانیہ کی اجازہ پہلی کے نکاح کو باطل کر دیتی ہے تو آخر نے اول کے حکم کو متغیر کر دیا۔ لہذا امعطف کی صورت میں دونوں کا نکاح باطل ہو جائیگا۔ دامانی الاخبار بالاعتاق [؟] اعتاق کے مسئلہ میں جو شخص خبر دے رہا ہے کہ اعتق ابی ہذا تو یہ قول اس غلام کے کل کے عشق کا موجب ہے تم قوله وهذا پھر اس کا قول و ہذا تو یہ موجب ہے کہ تکث [؟] ان دو غلاموں میں منقسم ہو اور غلام اول کا بعض ازاد ہو فيكون مغير الاول الکلام تو یہ اول کام کیلئے مغیر ہے اور مغتر [؟] کا اعتبار اس وقت ہوتا ہے جب متصلاً واقع ہو بخلاف الامتين بخلاف امتین کے کہ وہاں آخر کلام مغیر الاول نہیں ہے کیونکہ اعتقت بده و بندہ میں اعتاق ثانیہ پہلی کے اعتاق کے لئے مغیر نہیں ہو سکتا لہذا یہاں آخر کلام مغیر الاول نہیں ہے اور مسئلہ اختین میں آخر کلام مغتر [؟] لا قول ہے لہذا موقوف على الآخر ہوگا۔ وتد ذكر في المجامع الحصیری جامع حصیری میں ذکر کیا کہ مسئلہ امتین اور مسئلہ اختین میں کوئی فرق نہیں بل انما جاء الفرق بلکہ فرق صرف اس بنا پر ہوا ہے کہ وضع مسئلہ میں اختلاف ہے دھوان في مسئلة الا متین اور وہ فرق یہ ہے کہ امتین کے مسئلہ میں مولیٰ کہتا ہے ہدہ حرة ونذه حرة عطف جملہ علی الجملہ ہے تو پہلے جملہ کے ساتھ لونڈی ازاد ہوئی اس کا نکاح صحیح ہو گیا اور دوسرے جملہ سے جب تک فارغ نہیں ہوتا تو نکاح الامتہ علی الحرة ہے تو یہ باطل ہو جائے گا اور مسئلہ اختیں میں کہتا ہے اجزات نکاح بده و بده به عطف مفرد على المفرد ہے ایک ہی اجازہ کے ساتھ دونوں نکاح جائز قرار دے رہا ہے فانه افراد لكل الم یعنی مسئلہ امتین میں ہر ایک لونڈی الگ تحریر کی ہے ۔ لہذا یہاں صدر کلام آخر پر موقوف نہیں ہے لہذا یہ مغیر نہیں ہوگا اور اختین کے مسئلہ میں ہر ایک کے لیے الگ الگ اجازہ نہیں بلکہ دونوں کی اجازة واحدہ ہے لہذا اول کلام موقوف على الآخر ہو گا لہذا دونوں کا نکاح باطل ہو جائے گا۔ حتى توافر دھنا اگر مسئلہ احتین میں الگ الگ اجازہ کرتا مثلاً کہتا اجزت نکاح ہده و اجزات نکاح ہدہ تو اولیٰ کا نکاح صحیح ہو جاتا ولو لم يفرد في الامتین اگر امتین میں تحریر الگ الگ نہ ہوتی بلکہ یوں کہتا اعتقت بده بده تو دونوں معا ازاد ہو جائیں اور نکاح دونوں کا صحیح ہو جاتا ۔
In the case of two sisters, permission for the second marriage invalidates the first marriage, so the last alters the ruling of the first. Therefore, with conjunction, both marriages become invalid. [Unclear: Dāmanī al-akhbār bil-i'tāq] In the matter of informing about emancipation, if a person reports that 'I have freed this son of mine,' then this statement causes [something] regarding that slave's entire [؟]; then his statement 'and this' causes it to be divided between the two slaves, and part of the first slave becomes free, so it becomes a changer of the first statement. Thus it is a changer for the first, and consideration of the changer is when it occurs immediately. Unlike the case of two slave-girls: there the last statement is not a changer for the first because in 'I have freed this one and this one,' the second emancipation cannot change the first emancipation. Hence here the last statement is not a changer for the first. And in the case of two sisters, the last statement is a changer for the first, so it depends on the last. And it is mentioned in al-Jāmi' al-Hișīrī that there is no difference between the case of two slave-girls and two sisters; rather the difference is only due to a difference in the formulation of the case. The difference is: In the case of two slave-girls, the master says, 'This one is free and this one is free' – that is conjunction of sentence upon sentence. So with the first sentence, the slave-girl becomes free, her marriage becomes valid; and he does not complete the second sentence except that [the marriage of] the slave-girl to a free woman is invalid. And in the case of two sisters, he says, 'I have permitted the marriage of this one and this one' – that is conjunction of individual upon individual. With a single permission, he validates both marriages. So he has singled out the word for each [؟]. In the case of two slave-girls, each slave-girl is written separately. Therefore here the first part does not depend on the last, so it is not a changer. And in the case of two sisters, there is not a separate permission for each, but a single permission for both, hence the first part depends on the last, so both marriages become invalid. Even if he had given separate permission in the case of two sisters, e.g., 'I have permitted the marriage of this one and I have permitted the marriage of this one,' then the first marriage would be valid. And if he had not given separate emancipation in the case of two slave-girls, but said, 'I have freed this one and this one,' then both would be freed together and both marriages would be valid.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage is a rule about how the type of grammatical conjunction (عطف) affects legal outcomes. The key distinction is between conjoining whole sentences (عطف جملة على جملة) and conjoining individual words (عطف مفرد على مفرد). In the case of two slave-girls, the master says 'هذه حرة وهذه حرة' – two separate sentences. Each sentence is independent; the second does not change the first. So the first slave-girl's emancipation is complete immediately, and her marriage remains valid (since she is now a free woman marrying a free man? Actually the text says 'نكاح الامة على الحرة' – the marriage of a slave-girl to a free woman, which is invalid. So after the first becomes free, the second is still a slave, and the marriage of a slave to a free woman is invalid. But the point is that the second sentence does not retroactively affect the first. In contrast, in the case of two sisters, the person says 'أجزت نكاح هذه وهذه' – a single permission conjoined by 'waw' between two words. This is a single act of permission for both; the second part is part of the same utterance. Hence, the first part depends on the second for completion; if the second is invalid (since you cannot marry two sisters simultaneously), the whole is invalid. The author also cites al-Jami' al-Hișīrī, which states that the difference is merely due to the difference in the wording of the problem, not a difference in principle. The passage then explores hypotheticals: if separate sentences were used in the sisters case ('أجزت نكاح هذه وأجزت نكاح هذه'), the first would be valid. If a single sentence-word conjunction were used in the slave-girls case ('أعتقت هذه وهذه'), both would be freed together, and both marriages would be valid. This demonstrates that the form of utterance dictates whether the second part modifies the first.

Key Terms
عطف جملة على جملة ('aṭf jumla ʿalā jumla): Conjoining two complete sentences with a conjunction, where each sentence is independent in its own right.
عطف مفرد على مفرد ('aṭf mufrad ʿalā mufrad): Conjoining two individual words (e.g., nouns) under a single predicate or verb, making them share the same government.
مغیر (mugīr): That which changes; a later statement that retroactively alters the ruling of an earlier statement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of two sisters, if one says 'أجزت نكاح هذه وأجزت نكاح هذه' (two separate sentences), what is the ruling?
A) Both marriages are invalid
B) The first marriage is valid, the second is invalid
C) Both marriages are valid
D) The first marriage is invalid, the second is valid

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul rule: Conjunction of whole sentences ('atf jumal) keeps each act independent; conjunction of words ('atf mufrad) merges them into a single act where the second can affect the first.

The Rule of Mushāraka in Conjunctive Conditional Clauses
Explains when a second clause shares the same condition without تقدير

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the Hanafi rule of mushāraka and APPLY it to identify when a condition is shared across conjunctive clauses and when estimation of a separate condition is required.

Core Idea
In conjunctive conditional clauses, the second clause shares the condition of the first unless unity of the completing element is impossible.

This lesson unpacks a fundamental usul rule regarding the interpretation of conjunctive sentences. When two clauses are joined by waw, the second often relies on the first for its completion. The Hanafi school presumes that the same completing element (mutammim) applies to both, avoiding unnecessary repetition. However, this presumption is rebutted when the completing element cannot be identical. We will explore the rule through the classic example of conditional divorce and the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conjunctive structure
Recognize when a second clause is joined by waw and depends on the first clause for its mutammim (e.g., result of a condition or predicate of a subject).
Look for compound sentences where the second part would be incomplete without the first.
2
Apply the default rule of mushāraka
The second clause shares the exact same mutammim as the first; no need to estimate a separate one.
This is the default: the conjunction allows sharing unless something prevents it.
3
Check the exception: impossibility of unity
If the mutammim cannot be the same (e.g., different actions or subjects), then a separate mutammim must be estimated.
Example: 'Zaid came and 'Amr' – the coming of each is a separate action.
4
Analyze the divorce example
Apply the rule to 'If you enter, you are divorced, and divorced, and divorced.' According to Imam Abu Hanifa, one condition suffices, so only one divorce occurs (for an unconsummated marriage). Contrast with the Sahibayn's view requiring separate conditions.
This shows the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نہیں ہوگی ہر ایک جملہ کا حکم الگ الگ حاصل ہوگا ۔ وانما تجب بھی یہ مشاکہ اس وقت واجب ہوتی ہے . اذا افتقر الآخر الى الدول جب آخر کلام محتاج الى الاول هو نبشارك الدول یعنی اس وقت آخر کلام اول کے ساتھ مشارک ہو جائے گا اس حصہ میں جس کے ساتھ اول متمم ہوا ہے اور یہ عموماً وہاں ہوتا ہے جہاں بذریعہ وا و خبر مبتدا پر یا جزاء شرط پر عطف ہو ۔ بعینہ اور ثانی کے لئے متم بعینہ وہی ہو گا جو اول کے لئے متمم ہے لا بتقدیر مثلہ اس مستم کی مثل کی تقدیر نہیں کی جائے گی ان لم يمتنع الاتحاد بشرطیکہ معطوف اور معطوف علیہ میں متم کا متحد ہونا ممتنع نہ ہو نجوان دخلت الدار فانت طالق وطالق وطالق اور دونوں آخری معطوفین مفتقر الى الاول ہیں اور ان کے لئے متم بعینہ وہی ان دخلت ہے جو اول میں مذکور ہے ۔ ہر ایک طالق کے ساتھ الگ الگ ان دخلت مقدر نہیں کرنا پڑیگا۔ یہی کہا لیس کتکرار قولہ ان دخلت فانت طالق جیسے یہی قول بمع شرط کے مکرر کیا جاتا یہ اس جیسا نہیں فلا يقع الثلث تو امام کے نزدیک غیر مدخولہ کو اس صورت میں تین طلاق واقع نہیں ہوں گی بلکہ اول کے ساتھ بائنہ ہو جائیگی ثانی اور ثالث لغو ہو جائنگی خانہ یمکن تو اس صورت میں ممکن ہے کہ یہ جزیہ کثیر ایک ہی شرط متحد کے ساتھ جو اول مذکور ہے ان دخلت الدار اسی کے ساتھ متعلق ہو جائینگی یہاں تقدیر مثل نہیں کرنی پڑے گی۔ یعنی ہر ایک کے لئے الگ الگ شرط کی تقدیر نہیں ہوگی ۔ حتی کہ اس کو یوں قرار دیا جائے کہ ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق جیسے کہ صاحبین کے نزدیک ہے امام کے نزدیک ایسے نہیں ہوگا۔ او تقدیرہ یعنی بعینہ متم واحد کافی نہیں ہو گا بلکہ اس کی مثل مقدر کرنی ہوگی یہ اس وقت ہو گا جب کہ اتحاد مستم ممتنع ہو۔ یہی کہا ان امتنع الی الاتحاد یعنی اتحاد المتهم نحو جاء في زيد وعمرو کیونکہ مجی زید غیر ہے نجی عمر کا لہذا اس مقام پر وجاء فی عمر کی تقدیر ہو گی ۔
The ruling of each sentence will not be obtained separately. Rather, this sharing becomes obligatory when the second is in need of the first: when the last speech needs the first, it shares with it in the part in which the first is completed. And this generally occurs where the conjunction with waw is on the predicate of the subject or on the result of the condition. Exactly the same 'mutammim' for the second will be what is 'mutammim' for the first, without estimating its like, provided the union of the 'mutammim' is not impossible. For example: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, and divorced, and divorced.' The last two conjuncts are in need of the first, and for them the exact 'mutammim' is 'if you enter' mentioned in the first. For each 'divorce', a separate 'if you enter' will not be estimated. It is not like repeating the saying 'If you enter, you are divorced.' So according to Imam [Abu Hanifa], in the case of an unconsummated marriage, three divorces will not occur; rather, she becomes divorced with the first, and the second and third are void. Here it is possible that these multiple parts are attached to the single condition mentioned first, 'if you enter the house'; estimation of a like is not needed. Instead, one could consider it like 'If you enter the house, you are divorced; if you enter the house, you are divorced; if you enter the house, you are divorced' as according to the two companions. According to Imam, it is not like that. Or estimation: i.e., the exact one 'mutammim' will not suffice, but rather its like will be estimated. This occurs when the union of the 'mutammim' is impossible. For example: 'Zaid came and 'Amr', because the coming of Zaid is different from the coming of 'Amr; so here the estimation is 'and 'Amr came'.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage explains a key rule of conjunction in conditional sentences. When two clauses are conjoined by waw (and), the second clause may share the same 'mutammim' (completing element, here the condition) as the first. For this to happen, the second clause must be dependent on the first, such that repeating the condition separately is unnecessary. The text illustrates with the example: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, and divorced, and divorced.' According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the condition (entering the house) applies to all three pronouncements of divorce without repetition. Therefore, for an unconsummated marriage, only one divorce occurs, and the rest are void. This is opposed to the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) who require each 'divorce' to have its own condition, leading to multiple divorces. The text further distinguishes cases where the mutammim cannot be the same, like 'Zaid came and 'Amr', because the action of coming is different for each subject; here a separate mutammim is estimated.

Key Terms
مشاركة (mushāraka): The rule that a conjoined clause shares the same completing element (mutammim) as the first
متمم (mutammim): The completing part, such as a condition or predicate, upon which the clause depends
تقدیر مثل (taqdīr mithl): Estimating a similar but separate mutammim for the second clause

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which of the following sentences does the rule of mushāraka NOT apply, requiring estimation of a separate mutammim?
A) "If you come, I will honor you and I will honor you."
B) "Zaid came and 'Amr."
C) "If you study, you will succeed and you will be praised."
D) "If you enter, you are divorced and you are divorced."

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule of mushāraka presumes shared conditions in conjunctive clauses unless the completing element cannot be unified, ensuring linguistic efficiency.

Shirkah in Conditional Sentences: The Hanafi Rule of Waw and Its Application to Zakat on Minors
Usul rule with fiqh application

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule of shirkah (sharing) with waw in conditional sentences to determine whether a second clause shares the condition, and use this rule to evaluate the Hanafi position on zakah on minors.

Core Idea
Waw in conditional sentences imposes a shared condition only when the second clause is dependent on the first (in power of a single word).

This passage weaves a fiqh dispute (zakah on minors) into a linguistic usul analysis. The Hanafi position that zakah is not obligatory on a minor is defended not by mere reference to the Qur'anic text but by a rational argument about the nature of 'ibadah mahdah. The opposing view is rebutted using the principle of shirkah, which governs how conjunctions with waw operate in conditional sentences. Understanding this rule will sharpen your ability to derive rulings from texts and to evaluate competing interpretations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Opposing Arguments
Extract the Hanafi position (zakah not wajib on minor because it is pure worship) and the opponent's argument (address includes minors, guardian can pay).
The opponent's argument relies on a share (shirkah) between the minor's ownership and the guardian's ability.
2
Locate the Hanafi Rebuttal Principle
The Hanafi rebuttal is that the opponent's shirkah is invalid because sharing requires the second clause to be dependent on the first – here, it is not.
This introduces the linguistic rule of shirkah with waw.
3
Analyse the Shirkah Rule via Examples
Work through the examples: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and my slave is free' (condition applies to both) vs. 'and Zayd is beaten, divorced' (condition does not apply). Identify the key criterion: the second clause must be in the 'power of a single word' (quwwah al-mufrad), i.e., dependent.
The example of 'Establish prayer and give zakah' shows waw for sequence only, not sharing.
4
Apply the Shirkah Rule to the Zakat Dispute
Show that the opponent's claim of shirkah between the minor's ownership and guardian's ability fails because the second clause (guardian can pay) is not dependent on the first in the required way.
This directly rebuts the opponent's evidence.
5
Contrast with 'Ushr and Sadaqat al-Fitr
Note why 'ushr and sadaqat al-fitr are wajib on minors: they contain an element of hardship (mu'nah), so they are not pure worship – the same shirkah reasoning does not block obligation.
This shows the nuance of the Hanafi position.

نہیں ہے لہذا آتوا الزکوۃ کا مخاطب بھی نہیں ہوگا لگنا نقول یعنی مسئلہ تو ہم احناف کے نزدیک ہے کہ زکوۃ صبی پر واجب نہیں لیکن دلیل ہمارے نزدیک قران فی النظم نہیں ہے بلکہ ہمارے نزدیک وجہ یہ ہے کہ افعا لا تجب الزكاة علی الصبی صبی پر زکوۃ اس لئے واجب نہیں کہ یہ عبادہ محضہ ہے یعنی اس کے اندر معنی مونتہ و مشقہ کو دخل نہیں ہے اور صبی عبادة محضہ کے وجوب کی اہلیہ نہیں رکھتا اس لئے زکوۃ اس پر واجب نہیں ہے لا للقران في النظم یعنی قران فی النظم یہ دلیل نہیں ہے ۔ عشر اور صدقۃ الفطر کے اندر عبادہ کے علاوہ مونتہ کا معنی بھی معتبر ہے لہذا یہ واجب علی الصبی ہوں گے ۔ والقائل بوجوب الزکوۃ اور وہ حضرات جو صبی پر وجوب زکوۃ کے قائل ہیں وہ کہتے ہیں کہ صلوۃ و زکوة کا خطاب صبیان کو بھی شامل ہے لیکن عقل وجوب صلوۃ سے صبیان کی تخصیص کرتا ہے کیونکہ یہ عباد بدنیہ ہے اور صبحی مشقہ جسمانیہ برداشت کرنے سے عجز کی وجہ سے مستثنیٰ ہے اور زکوہ عبادہ مالیہ ہے اور اس کا مال اس کے ادا کرنے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے تو سمکن ادار الولی عنہ اس کی طرف سے اس کا ولی مال صبی سے ادا کر سکتا ہے ۔ وهذا فاسد عندنا یعنی جمل میں ایجاب شرکتہ ہمارے نزدیک فاسد ہے لان الشركة کیونکہ شرکتہ اس وقت ثابت ہوتی ہے جب جملہ ثانیہ محتاج الی اولی ہو فقی قوله ان دخلت الدار ائز یعنی جب کہتا ہے ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق وعبدی حر تو عشق غلام بھی دخول دار کی شرط سے معلق ہو جائے گا کیونکہ حملہ ثانیہ بحکم مفرد ہے حکم افتقار میں لان الاصل في المواد الشركة چونکہ داد کی اصل وضع اشتراک کے لئے ہے اور یہ اس وقت ثابت ہو سکتی ہے جب مجدی حوا کی عطف جزا پر ڈالا جائے اگر چہ یہ جملہ فی حد ذاتہا نام ہے لیکن حکم افتقار میں بمنزلہ مفرد کے ہے لہذا اس کا مخطف جزا پر ہو گا تا کہ واو عاطفہ اپنی اصل وضع پر برقرار ر ہے تو عطف اسمیہ یعنی سعیدی خرو کا آپ جیسے اسمیہ انت طالق پر ہو گا اور یہ دونوں ایک ہی شرط دخول دار کے ساتھ معلق ہو جائیں گے بخلاف وضنتر تک طالق کے کہ یہاں خبر کو ظاہر کر دیا ہے تو اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ اس کا عطف انت طالق پر نہیں ہے ورنہ تو صرف وضر تک کہنا کافی تھا طالق کے اظہار کی ضرورت نہ متقی بنا یہ جملہ ثانیہ معلق بیشتر ورنہ ناکافی تھا کے اظہار کی ضرورت تھی یا جملہ ثانی نہیں ہوگا۔ خان اظهار الخبر هنا دليل عدم المشاركة في الجزا.
لما ذكر ان الشركة الخرجب یہ ذکر کیا کہ معطوف اور معطوف علیہ میں شرکتہ اس وقت ثابت ہوتی ہے جب جملہ ثانیہ مفتقر الی الاولی ہو تو اشکال وارد ہوتا ہے کہ ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق و عیدی حروف میں عبدی حرا جملہ تامہ ہے جو اپنے ماقبل کی طرف محتاج نہیں ہے لہذا مناسب تھا کہ یہ شرط مذکورہ کے ساتھ متعلق نہ ہوتا بلکہ یہ کلام مستقل ہو کر مجموع شرط و جزا پر عطف ہوتا۔ فاجاب بانعاني قوة المفرد تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ باوجود جملہ نامہ ہونے کے یہ سمنزلہ مفرد کے ہے کہ محتاج الی الاولی ہے کیونکہ اس کو جزا کے ساتھ جملہ اسمیہ ہونے میلی مناسبت حاصل ہے لہذا یہ امر مرجح ہے کہ اس کا عطف صرف جزا پر ہوتا کہ عطف اسمیہ علی الا سمیہ ہو لا علی مجموع الشرط والجن اکیونکہ اس صورت میں معطوفین کے مابین مناسبت مذکورہ ختم ہو جائے گی۔ فاذا کانت جب یہ معطوف على المجزا ہوا تو یہ قوت مفرد میں ہوگا ۔ لان جزاء الشرط کیونکہ جزائے شرط حملہ کا بعض حصہ ہوتا ہے جملہ نامہ نہیں ہوتا وايضا الواو للعطف اور یہ دوسری وجہ ہے حاصل یہ کہ واو عطف کے لئے ہے اور عطف میں شرکۃ اصل ہے فتحصل على الشركة لہذا جہاں تک ممکن ہو اس اصل کی رعایت کرتے ہوئے واد کو شرکتہ پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔ وھذا اذا کان المعطوف اور یہ اس وقت ہے جب کہ معطوف اپنے ماقبل کی طرف حقیقتاً محتاج ہو۔ کمانی المفرد جیسے کہ معطوف مفرد ہو۔ ارحکما یا معطوف اپنے ماقبال کی طرف حکما محتاج ہو یہ اس جملہ میں ہوتا ہے جس کو قوۃ مفرد میں اعتبار کرنا ممکن ہو اس وقت محمول علی الشرکۃ ہو گا تاکہ واو عطف اپنے اصل پر بقدر امکان جاری رہے اما اذالم ممکن جب شرکتہ پر محمول کرنا ممکن نہ ہو تو فلا تحمل پھر محمول علی الشرکتہ نہیں کیا جائیگا وهذا اذا كان المعطوف جملة لا تكون في قوة المفرد سياس وقت ہوگا جب معطوف ایسا جملہ ہو جو قوۃ مفرد میں نہیں ہے تو یہ اپنے ماقبل کی طرف اصلاً محتاج نہیں ہو گا کسانی اقيموا الصلاة والوا الزکوۃ میں تو یہاں و او صرف نسق و ترتیب کے لئے ہوگی شرکت نہیں ہو گی ففی قولہ ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق ومرتك طالق میں وضر تک طالق کو دونوں وجہ پر محمول کرنا ممکن تو ہے لكن اظهار الخبر ليكن لفظ و ممر تک کے ساتھ لفظ طالق کو بصورت خبر ظاہر کرنا اس کو ترجیح دیتا ہے کہ اس کا عطف مجموعی شرط و جزا پر ہو نہ صرف جزا پر لانه لوکان معطونا کیونکہ اگر یہ صرف جزا پر مطوف ہوتا تو و مر تک کہنا کافی تھا ساتھ لفظ طالق کے کہنے کی ضرورت نہ تھی تو و عیدی حرء میں عتق غلام متعلق بالشرط ہوگا بخلاف وضر تک طالق یہ متعلق بالشرط نہیں ہو گا وھذا جعلنا قولہ تعالیٰ ولا تقبلوا لهم شهادة ابدا حاصل یہ کہ لا تقبلوا جملہ انشائیہ ہے۔ اور اس کے ساتھ خطاب ائمہ کو ہے جیسے فاجلدوا انشائیہ ہے اور مخاطب اس کے ساتھ ائمہ ہیں۔ اسی مناسبت کی وجہ سے لا تقبلوا کا عطف جزا یعنی فاجلدوا پر ہوگا اور یہ دونوں امر حد قذف میں درج ہوں گے اور بخلاف اولئک ھم الفاسقون یہ جملہ خبریہ ہے اور اس کے ساتھ ائمہ مخاطب نہیں ہیں لہذا اس کا عطف جزا پر نہیں ہوگا ۔ وثمرہ ہذا نانی فی آخر فصل الاستثنا انشاء اللہ تعالیٰ ۔
It is not, therefore the addressee of 'and give zakah' will also not be. We say: the issue among us Hanafis is that zakah is not wajib upon a minor, but the proof according to us is not the Qur'anic arrangement; rather, according to us the reason is that acts: zakah is not wajib upon the minor because it is a pure worship, meaning the element of hardship and toil does not enter into it, and the minor is not qualified for the obligation of pure worship, therefore zakah is not wajib upon him, not due to the Qur'anic arrangement, meaning the Qur'anic arrangement is not the proof. 'Ushr and sadaqat al-fitr contain the meaning of hardship in addition to worship, therefore these will be wajib upon the minor. And those who say zakah is obligatory (and those gentlemen who claim obligation of zakah upon the minor) say that the address of prayer and zakah includes minors, but reason specifies minors from the obligation of prayer because it is a bodily worship, and the minor is exempt due to inability to bear physical exertion, and zakah is a financial worship, and his wealth has the capacity to perform it, so it is possible for the guardian to perform it on his behalf from the minor's wealth. And this is invalid according to us, meaning the inclusion of sharing (shirkah) in the sentence is invalid according to us because sharing is established only when the second sentence is in need of the first. For example, his saying: 'If you enter the house, then you are divorced and my slave is free' – then the freeing of the slave will also be suspended on the condition of entering the house, because the second sentence is in the ruling of a single word in the ruling of need, because the original principle in the material of sharing is that the origin of 'waw' is for sharing, and it can be established only when the second is made to depend on the first, even if it is a complete sentence in itself, but in the ruling of need it is like a single word, therefore its 'atf (conjunction) is on the result, so that the conjunctive waw remains on its original principle. So the conjunctive sentence, like 'and my slave is free', is conjoined to 'you are divorced', and both will be suspended on the same condition of entering the house. Contrary to 'and Zayd is beaten, divorced' – here the predicate (khabar) has been made apparent, so it is known that its 'atf is not on 'you are divorced', otherwise it would have been sufficient to say 'and Zayd is beaten' without the need to mention 'divorced'. Therefore this second sentence is not suspended on the condition. (Khan:) Making the predicate apparent here is evidence of non-participation in the result. When he mentioned that sharing (shirkah) is established between the conjoined and that to which it is conjoined only when the second sentence depends on the first, an objection arises: in 'If you enter the house, then you are divorced and my slave is free', 'my slave is free' is a complete sentence that is not in need of what precedes it, so it would be appropriate that it should not be connected to the mentioned condition, but rather be an independent statement conjoined to the entire condition and result. He answered: considering the power of a single word, he said that despite being a complete sentence, it is like a single word in that it is in need of the first, because it has a nominal sentence correspondence with the result, therefore this is a preponderant factor that its 'atf is only on the result, so that the conjunction of a nominal sentence upon a nominal sentence occurs, not upon the combination of condition and result, because in that case the mentioned correspondence between the conjoined elements would be lost. So when it is conjoined to the result, it will be in the power of a single word, because the result of a condition is part of the sentence, not a complete sentence. And also, waw is for conjunction, and in conjunction sharing is the original principle, so as much as possible this principle is observed, the waw is interpreted as sharing. And this is when the conjoined is actually in need of what precedes it, like a single word, i.e. the conjoined is grammatically singular. Or the conjoined is in need of what precedes it in ruling – this occurs in a sentence that can be considered in the power of a single word; then it is interpreted as sharing so that the conjunctive waw operates on its original principle as far as possible. But when it is not possible to interpret as sharing, then it is not interpreted as sharing. And this is when the conjoined is a sentence that is not in the power of a single word; then it is not in need of what precedes it at all, like 'Establish prayer and give zakah' – here the waw is only for sequence and order, not for sharing. So in his saying: 'If you enter the house, then you are divorced and Zayd is beaten, divorced' – 'and Zayd is beaten, divorced' can be interpreted in both ways, but making the predicate apparent, i.e. mentioning the word 'divorced' along with 'and Zayd is beaten' in the form of a predicate, gives preponderance to its being conjoined to the entire condition and result, not just the result, because if it were conjoined only to the result, it would have been sufficient to say 'and Zayd is beaten' without the need to mention the word 'divorced'. So in 'and my slave is free', the emancipation of the slave is related to the condition, contrary to 'and Zayd is beaten, divorced' – this is not related to the condition. And this is what we made of His statement the Exalted: 'And never accept from them any testimony ever after' – the summary is that 'do not accept' is a performative sentence, and the address with it is to the rulers, just as 'flog them' is performative and the addressees are the rulers. Due to this correspondence, the 'atf of 'do not accept' is on the result, i.e. 'flog them', and both are included in the command of the hadd of qadhf. Contrary to 'those are the evildoers' – this is a declarative sentence, and the rulers are not addressed with it, therefore its 'atf is not on the result. And the fruit of this will appear at the end of the chapter of exception, if Allah wills.

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul discussion combining a substantive fiqh dispute (zakah on minors) with a linguistic usul principle (shirkah in conditional sentences). The author first states the Hanafi ruling: zakah is not wajib on a minor because it is a pure worship ('ibadah mahdah) lacking the element of hardship (ma'na al-mu'nah), and a minor is not qualified for such obligations. He distinguishes 'ushr and sadaqat al-fitr which include hardship. He then presents the opposing view that zakah is wajib because the address of zakah includes minors, but reason excludes them from bodily worships like salah; since zakah is financial, the guardian can pay from the minor's wealth. The author refutes this as invalid (fasid), using the rule of shirkah: the second sentence (the guardian's ability to pay) must be dependent on the first (the minor's ownership) for sharing to occur, which is not the case. He then elaborates on the rule of waw in conditional sentences: when a second clause is in the 'power of a single word' (quwwah al-mufrad), it shares the condition; otherwise, waw merely indicates sequence. Examples from divorce and manumission clarify the rule. Finally, he applies it to the Quranic verse on qadhf (24:4): 'do not accept their testimony' is a performative sentence addressed to rulers, so it shares the condition with 'flog them'; whereas 'those are the evildoers' is declarative and does not share. The discussion will bear fruit in the chapter on istithna. This is a classic demonstration of Hanafi usul: combining rational argument (dalil 'aqli) with linguistic analysis and concrete fiqh applications.

Key Terms
شركة (shirkah): مشاركة الجملة الثانية للجملة الأولى في الحكم أو الشرط إذا كانت الجملة الثانية في قوة المفرد ومحتاجة إلى الأولى (Sharing of the second clause with the first in the ruling or condition when the second clause is in the power of a single word and dependent on the first)
قوة المفرد (quwwah al-mufrad): حالة تكون فيها الجملة بحكم الاسم المفرد من حيث الاحتياج إلى ما قبلها (The state where a sentence is treated like a single word in terms of dependency on what precedes it)
عبادة محضة (ibadah mahdah): العبادة التي لا معنى فيها للمؤنة ولا المشقة ظاهرة (Worship that has no element of hardship or visible exertion)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key condition for a second clause conjoined by waw to share the condition in a conditional sentence according to the Hanafi rule of shirkah?
A) The second clause must be a command.
B) The second clause must be in the power of a single word (quwwah al-mufrad) and dependent on the first.
C) The second clause must be a nominal sentence.
D) The second clause must be longer than the first.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule of shirkah with waw determines whether a second clause shares the condition, based on its dependency on the first clause, and this principle refines the understanding of obligations in both linguistic analysis and fiqh disputes.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
